Full preservation l] **Policy Dilemma: The 2026 Iran Conflict Escalation**

Six days into the US-Israeli conflict with Iran, the situation has reached a critical juncture. Iranian retaliation for airstrikes on Tehran and four other cities has closed the Strait of Hormuz, disrupting 20-30% of global oil shipments and threatening 100 million Gulf state residents, while Saudi Arabia considers joining the conflict after Iranian strikes.

**Plan A: Sustained US-Israeli Airstrikes** - Continue "continuous powerful strikes" for several weeks using direct munitions to degrade Iran's military without ground invasion. Benefits: Establishes air dominance, eliminated 49 Iranian leaders including Supreme Leader Khamenei, pressures Iran toward negotiations. Costs: 3 US troops killed, 3 jets downed, hundreds projected dead, skyrocketing oil prices. Risk: Gulf states joining widens to regional war.

**Plan B: Iranian Escalation** - Prolong Strait closure and expand proxy attacks via Hezbollah/Houthis against Gulf infrastructure to force diplomacy. Benefits: Creates leverage by pressuring US allies, raises diplomatic incentives as US casualties mount. Costs: Devastates Iran's economy (70% non-oil trade dependent), invites Gulf coalition retaliation, disrupts 21 million barrels/day globally.

Neither plan resolves the core problem: Plan A degrades Iran militarily but fails to end retaliation cycles; Plan B generates short-term pressure but cannot sustain economically while expanding the war regionally.

Full preservation l] **The Strait of Hormuz Maritime Crisis Policy Dilemma**

Iran is attacking maritime traffic through the Strait of Hormuz, threatening 21 million barrels of oil per day (21% of global consumption) in response to US-Israeli strikes that killed 49 senior Iranian leaders on February 28, 2026.

**Plan A: Continued Military Operations + Shipping Protection**
Continue US-Israeli strikes to destroy Iran's missile capabilities and naval assets while protecting shipping lanes. Benefits: Prevents Strait closure, protects global oil flow, eliminates threats to regional allies. Costs: Risk of 20-30% oil price spikes affecting 195+ countries, uncertain operation duration, potential escalation with Hezbollah and other Iranian proxies across the region.

**Plan B: Immediate Ceasefire + Negotiated Settlement**
Halt military operations and pursue diplomatic resolution through regional mediators like Qatar. Benefits: Immediately stops maritime attacks, prevents $50-100+ billion in global economic damage, creates space for negotiations on uranium enrichment, missile limits, and proxy support. Costs: Leaves Iranian military infrastructure intact, may embolden future Iranian aggression, unclear whether Iran will genuinely negotiate given their stated refusal to engage.

Neither plan adequately addresses the fundamental tension between immediate economic stability and long-term regional security deterrence.
